Necessary and Theoretical Knowledge: Distinction and Variation
Author clarifies that necessary and theoretical are attributes of created knowledge, addressing variability among knowers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the same proposition can be necessary for one knower and theoretical for another, and identify the two responses given in this gloss.

Core Idea
Necessary and theoretical are attributes of created knowledge, not of the proposition itself.

In the Islamic epistemological tradition, 'necessary' (badīhī) and 'theoretical' (naẓarī) are used to classify knowledge based on how it is acquired. But what if the same truth is self-evident to a prophet yet requires reflection for a scholar? This gloss addresses that very question, defending the classification while accounting for individual variation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
The gloss states that necessary and theoretical are attributes of created knowledge. Notice that this immediately limits the scope: divine knowledge is not subject to this classification.
2
Recognize the objection
The objection: If a proposition (e.g., 'the world is created') is theoretical for one person and necessary for another, then the notion of 'dependence on reflection' (tawaqquf) becomes meaningless. Find this objection in the Arabic.
The phrase 'فلا معنى للتوقف' signals the objection.
3
Analyze the first response (dafʿ)
The first response (dafʿ) holds that each person's knowledge is numerically distinct (مغاير بالشخص). Therefore, one instance of knowledge may depend on reflection while another does not. This preserves the classification without contradiction.
This is a sophisticated point: knowledge is an accident that inheres in a particular subject, so it can differ between subjects.
4
Examine the second response (modifying tawaqquf)
Alternatively, one can reinterpret 'dependence' (tawaqquf) itself. Perhaps it does not require literal reflection in every case but rather a typical or dispositional reliance. This allows for prophets whose 'holy power' renders theoretical truths intuitive.
The gloss ends with 'فتدبر' (so reflect), inviting the reader to ponder further.
5
Apply to an Islamic science example
In usul al-fiqh, the obligation of prayer (wujūb al-ṣalāh) is theoretical for most Muslims (they need evidence from Qur'an and sunnah), but for the Prophet ﷺ it was necessary knowledge. Explain how the two responses justify this variation.
This shows the practical relevance of the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «الحاشية»: البديهة والنظرية صفة العلم بل الحادث، ومن ثمت جوزوا لصاحب القوة القدسية أن النظريات بأسرها تصورية ضرورية عنده، فلا يرد بأن شيئا يكون نظريا عند شخص، وبديهيا عند آخر، فلا معنى للتوقف. وجه الدفع: أن علم كل واحد مغاير لعلم آخر بالشخص، فيجوز أن يتوقف أحدهما دون الآخر. وقد يجاب بالتصرف في معنى التوقف، فتدبر.
He said in the Gloss: 'Intuitive and theoretical are attributes of knowledge—rather, of temporal knowledge. And therefore, they allowed for the possessor of the holy power that all theoretical matters are necessary conceptions for him. So it is not an objection that a thing is theoretical for one person and intuitive for another, so that dependence [on reflection] would be meaningless. The dafʿ [response] is: that each person's knowledge is numerically distinct from another's knowledge, so it is permissible that one depends [on reflection] and the other does not. And it may be answered by modifying the meaning of 'dependence' (tawaqquf), so reflect.'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage, attributed to a gloss (ḥāshiya), clarifies that terms like 'badīhī' (necessary/intuitive) and 'naẓarī' (theoretical) are properties of created (temporal) knowledge. They do not apply to divine knowledge. The gloss then addresses an objection: if the same proposition (e.g., 'the world is created') is theoretical for one person and intuitive for another (like prophets who have 'holy power'), then the notion of 'dependence on reflection' (tawaqquf) seems meaningless. The response (dafʿ) is that each person's knowledge is a distinct mental state; what requires reflection for one may be directly known by another due to differences in intellectual capacity. Alternatively, one can reinterpret 'dependence' not as a necessary condition but as a typical process. This preserves the validity of the distinction while allowing for individual variation. The passage is an expansion probe, elaborating on the nature of necessary and theoretical knowledge.

Key Terms
القوة القدسية
التوقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the gloss, why is it not an objection that a proposition can be theoretical for one person and necessary for another?
A) Because such variation never actually occurs.
B) Because each person's knowledge is numerically distinct, so dependence can differ.
C) Because necessary and theoretical are attributes of the proposition itself.
D) Because prophets are not included in the classification.

Key Takeaway
Necessary and theoretical are attributes of created knowledge, and the same proposition can be necessary for one knower and theoretical for another without contradiction, because knowledge is individual and dependence on reflection can vary or be reinterpreted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the proposition 'The Qur'an is the word of Allah.' For a prophet, it is necessary knowledge; for a layperson, it is theoretical. Using the concepts from this gloss, write a paragraph explaining why this variation does not invalidate the classification.
?
Explain the two responses (dafʿ and modifying tawaqquf) in your own words. Then apply them to a fiqh example: the obligation of prayer is theoretical for most Muslims but was necessary for the Prophet ﷺ.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Primary Object of Acquisition: Knowledge or the Known?
Author asserts the primarily acquired is the known object and refines 'dependence'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between knowledge and the known object as the primary acquisition and explain the refined meaning of 'dependence' in this context.

Core Idea
The real goal of acquiring knowledge is the known object, not the knowledge itself.

This passage tackles a subtle philosophical question: when we say we 'acquire' knowledge, is the thing primarily acquired the knowledge itself or the thing known? The author presents the view of the verifiers, including al-Sayyid, who argue that the known object is primary. By following the argument, you will grasp the purpose of cognitive acts like definition and understand that 'dependence' in knowledge acquisition is not an absolute condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing views
Find where the author states that the initial view assumes the acquired is knowledge (العلم), and then report the verifiers' view that it is the known object (المعلوم).
2
Understand the justification for the verifiers' view
The text says it is evident 'for one who consults his conscience'. Then it gives the example of definition (التحديد): the purpose of defining man is to obtain the quiddity of man, not just to have a mental concept. The known object (the quiddity) is the goal.
3
Analyze the refinement of 'dependence'
The author clarifies that 'dependence' (التوقف) in the definition of acquired knowledge does not mean real dependence (i.e., that inference must always precede). Instead, it is a marker that inference typically occurs, even if knowledge could be obtained without it (as in prophetic knowledge).
The term 'المصَّرحِ لدخول الفاء' likely means something that necessitates the conditional 'fa', indicating typical correlation.
4
Consider the reliance on common usage
The passage ends with 'استند البعض لشيوع استعمال', noting that some scholars support this refined view based on common linguistic usage.
This part is incomplete in the source; it signals an additional argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن هذا اعلم: مبني على أن المكتسب بالذات العلم. وقد ذهب المحققون، ومنهم السيد قدس سره الشريف، إلى أن المكتسب بالذات المعلوم، وهو ظاهر عند من يراجع إلى وجدانه؛ فإن المقصود من التحديد - مثلا - هو حصول كنه الإنسان بأي شخص من أشخاص العلم كان، فحينئذ لا جواب إلا الأخير. وتفصيله: أنه ليس المراد بالتوقف التوقف الحقيقي، بل الأمر المصَرِّحُ لدخول الفاء، وإن أمكن حصوله بدونه واستند البعض لشيوع استعمال.
Know that this is based on [the view] that the primarily acquired is knowledge. And the verifiers, among them al-Sayyid (may his secret be sanctified), held that the primarily acquired is the known object, and this is evident for one who consults his conscience; for the purpose of definition, for example, is obtaining the quiddity of man through whichever individual of knowledge it may be. So then there is no answer except the last one. And its detail: that what is meant by 'dependence' is not real dependence, but the thing that necessitates the entry of the 'fa' [i.e., conditional], even if it can be obtained without it, and some rely on the commonness of usage.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the term 'acquired' (muktasab) refers to knowledge itself or to the object known. The author initially states that the view being considered assumes that the acquired is essentially knowledge. However, the 'verifiers' (muḥaqqiqūn), including al-Sayyid (likely al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani or al-Dawwani), argue that the primary object of acquisition is the known thing (ma'lum). This is intuitive: when one defines 'man', the goal is to obtain the essence (quiddity) of man through some act of knowledge; the knowledge itself is a means, not the end. Thus, the only adequate answer to an earlier problem is the last one (i.e., that 'dependence' is not literal). The author then elaborates: 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definition of acquired knowledge does not mean a necessary condition (i.e., that inference must always precede), but rather it is a 'marker' (muṣarriḥ) that inference typically occurs, even if the knowledge could be obtained without it (as in the case of prophets). Some scholars rely on common usage to support this. The passage is a critical refinement, correcting a naïve view about what is acquired.

Key Terms
المكتسب بالذات
التحديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the verifiers mentioned in the passage, what is the primarily acquired in the process of definition?
A) The knowledge of the definition.
B) The defined object (the quiddity).
C) The act of defining.
D) The mental concept of definition.

Key Takeaway
The primarily acquired in cognition is the known object, and 'dependence' on inference is a typical pattern, not an absolute condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the example of defining 'salah' (prayer) in fiqh, explain why the primary object of acquisition is the definition (i.e., the known quiddity) rather than the act of defining itself.
?
Reflect on the statement: 'Acquired knowledge depends on inference.' Show how the refined understanding of 'dependence' (as typical, not necessary) applies to the case of a scholar who knows a ruling by intuition without explicit reasoning.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

The Double Division of Knowledge
Author presents the two divisions of knowledge and defends the double classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two divisions of knowledge (tasawwur/tasdiq and daruri/nadari) and explain why the double classification is considered acceptable.

Core Idea
Knowledge is divided twice: once by mental operation and once by source of certainty.

The author opens the passage by presenting two ways to categorize knowledge: first into concept and assent, and second into necessary and theoretical. He immediately notes that applying both classifications to the same knowledge is not problematic. This lesson will help you parse this foundational division that structures the entire science of logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two divisions
Read the first sentence: 'إما أولا في تقسيم العلم إلى التصور والتصديق بالحصولي الحادث، أو ثانيا في تقسيمهما إلى الضروري والنظري بالتصور والتصديق الحادثين.' Identify the two pairs: (التصور, التصديق) and (الضروري, النظري).
The phrase 'بالحصولي الحادث' indicates these are about acquired, contingent knowledge.
2
Understand the double specification
The author says 'ولا يبالي بالتخصيص مرتين' — meaning we do not mind specifying the same thing twice. This is because the divisions are based on different criteria: one by type of cognition, the other by dependence on reflection.
3
Why is it acceptable?
Explain that tasawwur/tasdiq is about the form of knowledge (simple vs. compound with judgment), while daruri/nadari is about its epistemic basis (self-evident vs. derived). They are orthogonal classifications.
This prepares the ground for later debates on divine knowledge and individual differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إما أولا في تقسيم العلم إلى التصور والتصديق بالحصولي الحادث، أو ثانيا في تقسيمهما إلى الضروري والنظري بالتصور والتصديق الحادثين، ولا يبالي بالتخصيص مرتين، وهو الأظهر. وما قيل: إن علم الواجب سبحانه لا يكون تصورا وتصديقا، إن أريد أنه تعالى ليس مصدقا للصوادق، كما يلوح من الأسفار الأربعة، فهو باطل، بل هو كفر صريح. وإن أريد مجرد الاصطلاح لعدم تعلق الغرض العلمي بالعلم القديم فلا مشاحة فيه، لكن لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون العلم القديم تصورا وتصديقا. قال في «الحاشية»: البديهة والنظرية صفة العلم بل الحادث، ومن ثمت جوزوا لصاحب القوة القدسية أن النظريات بأسرها تصورية ضرورية عنده، فلا يرد بأن شيئا يكون نظريا عند شخص، وبديهيا عند آخر، فلا معنى للتوقف. وجه الدفع: أن علم كل واحد مغاير لعلم آخر بالشخص، فيجوز أن يتوقف أحدهما دون الآخر. وقد يجاب بالتصرف في معنى التوقف، فتدبر. : أن هذا اعلم: مبني على أن المكتسب بالذات العلم. وقد ذهب المحققون، ومنهم السيد قدس سره الشريف، إلى أن المكتسب بالذات المعلوم، وهو ظاهر عند من يراجع إلى وجدانه؛ فإن المقصود من التحديد - مثلا ـ هو حصول كنه الإنسان بأي شخص من أشخاص العلم كان، فحينئذ لا جواب إلا الأخير. وتفصيله: أنه ليس المراد بالتوقف التوقف الحقيقي، بل الأمر المصَرِّحُ لدخول الفاء، وإن أمكن حصوله بدونه واستند البعض لشيوع استعمال التوقف بهذا المعنى في كلامهم؛ فإنهم جوزوا تبادل العلة المستقلة على معلول واحد شخصي، مع إطلاق لفظ التوقف فيها، مع إمكان وجود المعلول بدون كل واحد منها، وليس الجواب موقوفا على هذا كما ظن؛ فإن هذا غلط فاحش. وقال هذا الظان الجليل في الجواب إن المراد في تعريف الكسبي من الحصول مطلق الحصول، وفي تعريف الضروري الحصول المطلق، فالنظري ما يتوقف حصول في الجملة على النظر، والضروري ما لا يتوقف جميع أنحاء حصولاته على النظر، فما يحصل لواحد بالنظر يكون نظريا دائما، وإن حصل آخر بلا نظر، وإنما الضروري ما يحصل لكل واحد من غير نظر(١)، ولا يخفى ما فيه؛ إذ لو كان هو المصطلح من عند نفسه فلا مشاحة، لكن الإشكال باق على ما هو مقرر عند القوم. وإن زعم أن مراد القوم هو هذا كما هو ظاهر كلامه فباطل، وإلا لم يتم الدليل الآتي، ولا يستقيم قولهم: مبادئ البرهان أن تكون ضرورية أو منتهية إليها ولكان أكثر المصادرات الهندسية نظرية، إلى غير ذلك من المفاسد كما لا يخفى على المتدرب، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. (١) ولم أجد في كلام الدواني في شرح التهذيب هذا الذي نقله عنه الشارح، ولا في حاشية الشمسية، ولعله في كتاب آخر له، والله أعلم.
Either first: dividing knowledge into concept and assent by way of acquired (hadith) occurrence, or second: dividing them into necessary and theoretical by way of the occurring concept and assent, and no attention is paid to the double specification, and that is the more apparent. And what is said: that the knowledge of the Necessary Exalted is not concept and assent, if it is intended that He Most High is not an assenter to true propositions, as appears from the Four Journeys, then it is false, rather it is explicit disbelief. And if it is intended merely terminological convention due to the lack of scientific interest in eternal knowledge, then there is no dispute in it, but it does not necessarily imply that eternal knowledge is not concept and assent. He said in ‘al-Hashiya’: The intuitive and the theoretical are attributes of knowledge, rather the originated knowledge, and from that they permitted for the possessor of the holy power that all theoretical things are conceptive necessary for him, so it cannot be objected that something is theoretical for one person and intuitive for another, so there is no meaning to dependence. The way of rebuttal: that the knowledge of each one is individually different from another knowledge, so it is permissible that one depends and the other does not. And it might be answered by manipulation in the meaning of dependence, so reflect. This is based on the fact that the essentially acquired is the knowledge. And the verifiers, among them al-Sayyid (may Allah sanctify his noble secret), held that the essentially acquired is the known object, and it is apparent to whoever consults his conscience; for the purpose of definition, for example, is the attainment of the quiddity of man by any individual of the individuals of knowledge, so then there is no answer except the latter. Its detail: that the intended meaning of dependence is not real dependence, but rather the matter that necessitates the entry of the fa’, even if its attainment is possible without it, and some relied on the common usage of dependence in this sense in their speech; for they allowed the exchange of independent cause on a single individual effect, while using the word dependence therein, despite the possibility of the effect existing without each one of them. And the answer is not dependent on this as was thought; for this is a gross error. And this noble thinker said in the answer that the intended meaning in the definition of the acquired from ‘occurrence’ is absolute occurrence, and in the definition of the necessary is the absolute occurrence, so the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection, and the necessary is that all aspects of whose occurrences do not depend on reflection, so what is obtained for one by reflection is always theoretical, even if another is obtained without reflection, and the necessary is what is obtained for everyone without reflection(1). And it is not hidden what is in it; for if it was his own convention, then no dispute, but the problem remains on what is established with the people. And if he claims that the intended meaning of the people is this as apparent from his speech, then it is false, otherwise the following proof would not be complete, and their statement ‘the principles of demonstration must be necessary or terminating to it’ would not be correct, and most geometrical postulates would be theoretical, and other corruptions as is not hidden from the trained. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. (1) And I did not find in the speech of al-Dawani in his commentary on al-Tahdhib this which the commentator transmitted from him, nor in the Hashiya on al-Shamsiyya, perhaps it is in another book of his. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a compressed matn line from al-Sullam about the division of knowledge. The author first states that knowledge can be divided either first into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), or second into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nadari). He notes that the preferred view is not to mind the double classification. He then addresses an objection about divine knowledge: some claimed Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. He refutes this, saying if it means Allah does not assent to truths, it is disbelief; if it's just terminology, it's permissible but does not negate that His knowledge could be called concept and assent. He cites a hashia stating that 'intuitive' and 'theoretical' apply only to originated knowledge, not eternal. This allows that for a person with holy power (like a prophet), all theoretical matters may be intuitive, so something can be theoretical for one person and intuitive for another without contradiction. The rebuttal is that each person's knowledge is individually distinct, so one may depend on reflection and another not. Next, the author discusses a deeper issue: whether the essentially acquired thing in knowledge acquisition is the knowledge itself or the known object. The verifiers (muhaqqiqun, including al-Sayyid) hold it is the known object, as the purpose of definition is to attain the quiddity, not the knowledge. He then clarifies the meaning of 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definitions: it is not real dependence but a conditional necessity (like the entry of 'fa' in a conditional statement). Some scholars allowed independent causes for a single effect while still using 'dependence' loosely. The author criticizes a certain thinker's proposed solution that the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection and the necessary is that all aspects of which do not depend. He dismisses this as a mere terminological change that fails to solve the real issue, because if taken as the people's intended meaning, it would break the standard proof that the principles of demonstration must be necessary, and would render most geometrical postulates theoretical, leading to absurdities. The author concludes with 'Allah knows best,' and a footnote notes that the attributed view of al-Dawani is not found in his works.

Key Terms
التصور
التصديق
الضروري
النظري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the double specification (dividing the same knowledge twice) acceptable?
A) Because the two divisions are actually the same.
B) Because they are based on different criteria: the first on mental operation, the second on epistemic dependence.
C) Because the author is ignoring the logical rule of classification.
D) Because tasawwur and tasdiq are the same as daruri and nadari.

Key Takeaway
The two divisions of knowledge are complementary: tasawwur/tasdiq and daruri/nadari, and they are applied to acquired knowledge without conflict.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a classification tree for knowledge: start with 'acquired knowledge', branch into tasawwur and tasdiq, and also into daruri and nadari. Explain how these classifications intersect.

Divine Knowledge and the Objection
Author refutes an objection that divine knowledge is not concept and assent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the claim that Allah's knowledge is not tasawwur and tasdiq, distinguishing between a theological error and a mere terminological dispute.

Core Idea
Denying that Allah has assent is disbelief; denying the term is just convention.

The passage addresses an objection: some argue that Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. The author responds with a sharp distinction. If the claim is that Allah does not assent to truths, it is kufr. If it is merely about terminology, it is permissible but does not negate the reality. This lesson equips you to spot theological pitfalls in logical definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states: 'إن علم الواجب سبحانه لا يكون تصورا وتصديقا' — Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. Locate this phrase in the Arabic.
2
Analyze the two interpretations
The author splits the claim: if it means Allah is not an assenter (مصدق) to true propositions, it is false and kufr. If it is just a terminological choice (اصطلاح) because we don't scientifically investigate eternal knowledge, then it's a harmless convention.
The phrase 'كما يلوح من الأسفار الأربعة' refers to a work (al-Asfar al-Arba‘a) that might imply the first interpretation.
3
Evaluate the consequence
The author notes that even if we adopt the terminological restriction, it does not logically entail that eternal knowledge is not concept and assent in reality. So the objection fails to undermine the classification.

Either first: dividing knowledge into concept and assent by way of acquired (hadith) occurrence, or second: dividing them into necessary and theoretical by way of the occurring concept and assent, and no attention is paid to the double specification, and that is the more apparent. And what is said: that the knowledge of the Necessary Exalted is not concept and assent, if it is intended that He Most High is not an assenter to true propositions, as appears from the Four Journeys, then it is false, rather it is explicit disbelief. And if it is intended merely terminological convention due to the lack of scientific interest in eternal knowledge, then there is no dispute in it, but it does not necessarily imply that eternal knowledge is not concept and assent. The way of rebuttal: that the knowledge of each one is individually different from another knowledge, so it is permissible that one depends and the other does not. And it might be answered by manipulation in the meaning of dependence, so reflect. This is based on the fact that the essentially acquired is the knowledge. And the verifiers, among them al-Sayyid (may Allah sanctify his noble secret), held that the essentially acquired is the known object, and it is apparent to whoever consults his conscience; for the purpose of definition, for example, is the attainment of the quiddity of man by any individual of the individuals of knowledge, so then there is no answer except the latter. And this noble thinker said in the answer that the intended meaning in the definition of the acquired from ‘occurrence’ is absolute occurrence, and in the definition of the necessary is the absolute occurrence, so the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection, and the necessary is that all aspects of whose occurrences do not depend on reflection, so what is obtained for one by reflection is always theoretical, even if another is obtained without reflection, and the necessary is what is obtained for everyone without reflection(1). And if he claims that the intended meaning of the people is this as apparent from his speech, then it is false, otherwise the following proof would not be complete, and their statement ‘the principles of demonstration must be necessary or terminating to it’ would not be correct, and most geometrical postulates would be theoretical, and other corruptions as is not hidden from the trained. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. (1) And I did not find in the speech of al-Dawani in his commentary on al-Tahdhib this which the commentator transmitted from him, nor in the Hashiya on al-Shamsiyya, perhaps it is in another book of his. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a compressed matn line from al-Sullam about the division of knowledge. The author first states that knowledge can be divided either first into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), or second into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nadari). He notes that the preferred view is not to mind the double classification. He then addresses an objection about divine knowledge: some claimed Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. He refutes this, saying if it means Allah does not assent to truths, it is disbelief; if it's just terminology, it's permissible but does not negate that His knowledge could be called concept and assent. He cites a hashia stating that 'intuitive' and 'theoretical' apply only to originated knowledge, not eternal. This allows that for a person with holy power (like a prophet), all theoretical matters may be intuitive, so something can be theoretical for one person and intuitive for another without contradiction. The rebuttal is that each person's knowledge is individually distinct, so one may depend on reflection and another not. Next, the author discusses a deeper issue: whether the essentially acquired thing in knowledge acquisition is the knowledge itself or the known object. The verifiers (muhaqqiqun, including al-Sayyid) hold it is the known object, as the purpose of definition is to attain the quiddity, not the knowledge. He then clarifies the meaning of 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definitions: it is not real dependence but a conditional necessity (like the entry of 'fa' in a conditional statement). Some scholars allowed independent causes for a single effect while still using 'dependence' loosely. The author criticizes a certain thinker's proposed solution that the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection and the necessary is that all aspects of which do not depend. He dismisses this as a mere terminological change that fails to solve the real issue, because if taken as the people's intended meaning, it would break the standard proof that the principles of demonstration must be necessary, and would render most geometrical postulates theoretical, leading to absurdities. The author concludes with 'Allah knows best,' and a footnote notes that the attributed view of al-Dawani is not found in his works.

Key Terms
علم الواجب
مصدق
اصطلاح
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, if someone says 'Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent' meaning Allah does not assent to true propositions, what is the ruling?
A) It is a permissible terminological choice.
B) It is a false statement but not disbelief.
C) It is explicit disbelief (kufr sarih).
D) It is correct because God's knowledge is beyond categories.

Key Takeaway
When dealing with divine attributes in logic, distinguish between denying the reality (which is theological error) and merely restricting the terminology (which is permissible but inconclusive).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the claim 'Allah does not have tasawwur because He knows all things at once without concepts'. Using the distinction in this lesson, evaluate whether this claim is theological or terminological. Write a brief response.

Individual Variation and Dependence
Author explains how the same thing can be necessary for one and theoretical for another.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why something can be theoretical for one person and necessary for another, using the concept of tawaqquf and the individuality of knowledge.

Core Idea
Knowledge is individual; one person's necessary is another's theoretical.

The passage addresses an important nuance: the same proposition may be necessary (self-evident) for one person and theoretical (requiring proof) for another. This is possible because each person's knowledge is a distinct mental event. The author also introduces a subtle reinterpretation of 'dependence' as conditional necessity. This lesson will help you grasp this key principle in Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The problem is that if necessary and theoretical are defined by dependence on reflection, then the same thing could be both for different people, which seems contradictory. Locate the phrase: 'فلا يرد بأن شيئا يكون نظريا عند شخص، وبديهيا عند آخر، فلا معنى للتوقف.'
2
Understand the first answer: individual differences
The author gives a rebuttal: 'أن علم كل واحد مغاير لعلم آخر بالشخص، فيجوز أن يتوقف أحدهما دون الآخر.' Each person's knowledge is a different individual instance, so one can depend and another not.
3
Consider the second answer: manipulation of tawaqquf
The author mentions another answer: manipulate the meaning of dependence (تصرف في معنى التوقف). This leads to the discussion of tawaqquf as conditional necessity, not real dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إما أولا في تقسيم العلم إلى التصور والتصديق بالحصولي الحادث، أو ثانيا في تقسيمهما إلى الضروري والنظري بالتصور والتصديق الحادثين، ولا يبالي بالتخصيص مرتين، وهو الأظهر. وما قيل: إن علم الواجب سبحانه لا يكون تصورا وتصديقا، إن أريد أنه تعالى ليس مصدقا للصوادق، كما يلوح من الأسفار الأربعة، فهو باطل، بل هو كفر صريح. وإن أريد مجرد الاصطلاح لعدم تعلق الغرض العلمي بالعلم القديم فلا مشاحة فيه، لكن لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون العلم القديم تصورا وتصديقا. قال في «الحاشية»: البديهة والنظرية صفة العلم بل الحادث، ومن ثمت جوزوا لصاحب القوة القدسية أن النظريات بأسرها تصورية ضرورية عنده، فلا يرد بأن شيئا يكون نظريا عند شخص، وبديهيا عند آخر، فلا معنى للتوقف. وجه الدفع: أن علم كل واحد مغاير لعلم آخر بالشخص، فيجوز أن يتوقف أحدهما دون الآخر. وقد يجاب بالتصرف في معنى التوقف، فتدبر. : أن هذا اعلم: مبني على أن المكتسب بالذات العلم. وقد ذهب المحققون، ومنهم السيد قدس سره الشريف، إلى أن المكتسب بالذات المعلوم، وهو ظاهر عند من يراجع إلى وجدانه؛ فإن المقصود من التحديد - مثلا ـ هو حصول كنه الإنسان بأي شخص من أشخاص العلم كان، فحينئذ لا جواب إلا الأخير. وتفصيله: أنه ليس المراد بالتوقف التوقف الحقيقي، بل الأمر المصَرِّحُ لدخول الفاء، وإن أمكن حصوله بدونه واستند البعض لشيوع استعمال التوقف بهذا المعنى في كلامهم؛ فإنهم جوزوا تبادل العلة المستقلة على معلول واحد شخصي، مع إطلاق لفظ التوقف فيها، مع إمكان وجود المعلول بدون كل واحد منها، وليس الجواب موقوفا على هذا كما ظن؛ فإن هذا غلط فاحش. وقال هذا الظان الجليل في الجواب إن المراد في تعريف الكسبي من الحصول مطلق الحصول، وفي تعريف الضروري الحصول المطلق، فالنظري ما يتوقف حصول في الجملة على النظر، والضروري ما لا يتوقف جميع أنحاء حصولاته على النظر، فما يحصل لواحد بالنظر يكون نظريا دائما، وإن حصل آخر بلا نظر، وإنما الضروري ما يحصل لكل واحد من غير نظر(١)، ولا يخفى ما فيه؛ إذ لو كان هو المصطلح من عند نفسه فلا مشاحة، لكن الإشكال باق على ما هو مقرر عند القوم. وإن زعم أن مراد القوم هو هذا كما هو ظاهر كلامه فباطل، وإلا لم يتم الدليل الآتي، ولا يستقيم قولهم: مبادئ البرهان أن تكون ضرورية أو منتهية إليها ولكان أكثر المصادرات الهندسية نظرية، إلى غير ذلك من المفاسد كما لا يخفى على المتدرب، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. (١) ولم أجد في كلام الدواني في شرح التهذيب هذا الذي نقله عنه الشارح، ولا في حاشية الشمسية، ولعله في كتاب آخر له، والله أعلم.
Either first: dividing knowledge into concept and assent by way of acquired (hadith) occurrence, or second: dividing them into necessary and theoretical by way of the occurring concept and assent, and no attention is paid to the double specification, and that is the more apparent. And what is said: that the knowledge of the Necessary Exalted is not concept and assent, if it is intended that He Most High is not an assenter to true propositions, as appears from the Four Journeys, then it is false, rather it is explicit disbelief. And if it is intended merely terminological convention due to the lack of scientific interest in eternal knowledge, then there is no dispute in it, but it does not necessarily imply that eternal knowledge is not concept and assent. He said in ‘al-Hashiya’: The intuitive and the theoretical are attributes of knowledge, rather the originated knowledge, and from that they permitted for the possessor of the holy power that all theoretical things are conceptive necessary for him, so it cannot be objected that something is theoretical for one person and intuitive for another, so there is no meaning to dependence. The way of rebuttal: that the knowledge of each one is individually different from another knowledge, so it is permissible that one depends and the other does not. And it might be answered by manipulation in the meaning of dependence, so reflect. This is based on the fact that the essentially acquired is the knowledge. And the verifiers, among them al-Sayyid (may Allah sanctify his noble secret), held that the essentially acquired is the known object, and it is apparent to whoever consults his conscience; for the purpose of definition, for example, is the attainment of the quiddity of man by any individual of the individuals of knowledge, so then there is no answer except the latter. Its detail: that the intended meaning of dependence is not real dependence, but rather the matter that necessitates the entry of the fa’, even if its attainment is possible without it, and some relied on the common usage of dependence in this sense in their speech; for they allowed the exchange of independent cause on a single individual effect, while using the word dependence therein, despite the possibility of the effect existing without each one of them. And the answer is not dependent on this as was thought; for this is a gross error. And this noble thinker said in the answer that the intended meaning in the definition of the acquired from ‘occurrence’ is absolute occurrence, and in the definition of the necessary is the absolute occurrence, so the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection, and the necessary is that all aspects of whose occurrences do not depend on reflection, so what is obtained for one by reflection is always theoretical, even if another is obtained without reflection, and the necessary is what is obtained for everyone without reflection(1). And it is not hidden what is in it; for if it was his own convention, then no dispute, but the problem remains on what is established with the people. And if he claims that the intended meaning of the people is this as apparent from his speech, then it is false, otherwise the following proof would not be complete, and their statement ‘the principles of demonstration must be necessary or terminating to it’ would not be correct, and most geometrical postulates would be theoretical, and other corruptions as is not hidden from the trained. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. (1) And I did not find in the speech of al-Dawani in his commentary on al-Tahdhib this which the commentator transmitted from him, nor in the Hashiya on al-Shamsiyya, perhaps it is in another book of his. And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a compressed matn line from al-Sullam about the division of knowledge. The author first states that knowledge can be divided either first into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), or second into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nadari). The Essentially Acquired is the Known Object
Author argues that the essentially acquired in knowledge is the known object.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to argue for the position that the essentially acquired thing in knowledge acquisition is the known object (al-malum) rather than the knowledge itself.

Core Idea
The purpose of knowledge is to attain the known, not the act of knowing.

The passage dives into a subtle metaphysical question: when we acquire knowledge, what is essentially acquired? Is it the knowledge itself (the mental form) or the known object (the thing known)? The author sides with the verifiers (muhaqqiqun) that it is the known object, because the purpose of definition is to grasp the quiddity of the thing, not the mental picture. This lesson will walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage says: 'هذا مبني على أن المكتسب بالذات العلم. وقد ذهب المحققون، ومنهم السيد قدس سره الشريف، إلى أن المكتسب بالذات المعلوم.' One view: the acquired is the knowledge. The other: the acquired is the known object.
The author sides with the latter.
2
Understand the argument from purpose
The author gives an example: 'فإن المقصود من التحديد - مثلا ـ هو حصول كنه الإنسان' — the goal of definition is to attain the essence of man. So the object sought is the known essence, not the mental concept.
3
Recognize the consequence for the definition of dependence
If the essential acquisition is the known object, then the earlier discussion on tawaqquf must be reinterpreted. The author says 'فلا جواب إلا الأخير' meaning only the last answer (manipulation of tawaqquf) remains.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a compressed matn line from al-Sullam about the division of knowledge. The author first states that knowledge can be divided either first into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), or second into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nadari). He notes that the preferred view is not to mind the double classification. He then addresses an objection about divine knowledge: some claimed Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. He refutes this, saying if it means Allah does not assent to truths, it is disbelief; if it's just terminology, it's permissible but does not negate that His knowledge could be called concept and assent. He cites a hashia stating that 'intuitive' and 'theoretical' apply only to originated knowledge, not eternal. This allows that for a person with holy power (like a prophet), all theoretical matters may be intuitive, so something can be theoretical for one person and intuitive for another without contradiction. The rebuttal is that each person's knowledge is individually distinct, so one may depend on reflection and another not. Next, the author discusses a deeper issue: whether the essentially acquired thing in knowledge acquisition is the knowledge itself or the known object. The verifiers (muhaqqiqun, including al-Sayyid) hold it is the known object, as the purpose of definition is to attain the quiddity, not the knowledge. He then clarifies the meaning of 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definitions: it is not real dependence but a conditional necessity (like the entry of 'fa' in a conditional statement). Some scholars allowed independent causes for a single effect while still using 'dependence' loosely. The author criticizes a certain thinker's proposed solution that the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection and the necessary is that all aspects of which do not depend. He dismisses this as a mere terminological change that fails to solve the real issue, because if taken as the people's intended meaning, it would break the standard proof that the principles of demonstration must be necessary, and would render most geometrical postulates theoretical, leading to absurdities. The author concludes with 'Allah knows best,' and a footnote notes that the attributed view of al-Dawani is not found in his works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the process of performing ijtihad: a mujtahid uses evidence to arrive at a ruling. According to the muhaqqiqun's view, what is the essentially acquired? Write a brief defense of the position.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
9 min
The Meaning of Dependence (Tawaqquf)
Author clarifies that 'dependence' in the definitions is not real but conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real dependence and conditional necessity (like the 'fa') in defining necessary and theoretical knowledge.

Core Idea
Dependence in these definitions is not causal but conditional: it is the condition for the 'fa'.

A crucial clarification in the passage is that 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definitions of necessary and theoretical knowledge is not real, causal dependence. Instead, it is a conditional necessity analogous to the entry of the letter 'fa' in Arabic (e.g., 'if A, then B' means B depends on A conceptually, not necessarily causally). This lesson unpacks this subtle but important point.

Guided Path
1
Locate the clarification
The passage states: 'أنه ليس المراد بالتوقف التوقف الحقيقي، بل الأمر المصَرِّحُ لدخول الفاء' — the intended meaning is not real dependence but the matter that necessitates the entry of the 'fa'.
2
Understand the analogy with independent causes
The author mentions that logicians allow 'exchange of independent cause on a single effect' while still using 'dependence', showing that dependence can be loose.
3
Recognize the consequence
With this reinterpretation, the definitions become: theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum is conditioned by reflection (like 'if reflection, then knowledge'), and necessary is that whose occurrence is not conditioned by reflection in any aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إما أولا في تقسيم العلم إلى التصور والتصديق بالحصولي الحادث، أو ثانيا في تقسيمهما إلى الضروري والنظري بالتصور والتصديق الحادثين، ولا يبالي بالتخصيص مرتين، وهو الأظهر. وما قيل: إن علم الواجب سبحانه لا يكون تصورا وتصديقا، إن أريد أنه تعالى ليس مصدقا للصوادق، كما يلوح من الأسفار الأربعة، فهو باطل، بل هو كفر صريح. وإن أريد مجرد الاصطلاح لعدم تعلق الغرض العلمي بالعلم القديم فلا مشاحة فيه، لكن لا يلزم منه أن لا يكون العلم القديم تصورا وتصديقا. قال في «الحاشية»: البديهة والنظرية صفة العلم بل الحادث، ومن ثمت جوزوا لصاحب القوة القدسية أن النظريات بأسرها تصورية ضرورية عنده، فلا يرد بأن شيئا يكون نظريا عند شخص، وبديهيا عند آخر، فلا معنى للتوقف. وجه الدفع: أن علم كل واحد مغاير لعلم آخر بالشخص، فيجوز أن يتوقف أحدهما دون الآخر. وقد يجاب بالتصرف في معنى التوقف، فتدبر. : أن هذا اعلم: مبني على أن المكتسب بالذات العلم. وقد ذهب المحققون، ومنهم السيد قدس سره الشريف، إلى أن المكتسب بالذات المعلوم، وهو ظاهر عند من يراجع إلى وجدانه؛ فإن المقصود من التحديد - مثلا ـ هو حصول كنه الإنسان بأي شخص من أشخاص العلم كان، فحينئذ لا جواب إلا الأخير. وتفصيله: أنه ليس المراد بالتوقف التوقف الحقيقي، بل الأمر المصَرِّحُ لدخول الفاء، وإن أمكن حصوله بدونه واستند البعض لشيوع استعمال التوقف بهذا المعنى في كلامهم؛ فإنهم جوزوا تبادل العلة المستقلة على معلول واحد شخصي، مع إطلاق لفظ التوقف فيها، مع إمكان وجود المعلول بدون كل واحد منها، وليس الجواب موقوفا على هذا كما ظن؛ فإن هذا غلط فاحش. وقال هذا الظان الجليل في الجواب إن المراد في تعريف الكسبي من الحصول مطلق الحصول، وفي تعريف الضروري الحصول المطلق، فالنظري ما يتوقف حصول في الجملة على النظر، والضروري ما لا يتوقف جميع أنحاء حصولاته على النظر، فما يحصل لواحد بالنظر يكون نظريا دائما، وإن حصل آخر بلا نظر، وإنما الضروري ما يحصل لكل واحد من غير نظر(١)، ولا يخفى ما فيه؛ إذ لو كان هو المصطلح من عند نفسه فلا مشاحة، لكن الإشكال باق على ما هو مقرر عند القوم. وإن زعم أن مراد القوم هو هذا كما هو ظاهر كلامه فباطل، وإلا لم يتم الدليل الآتي، ولا يستقيم قولهم: مبادئ البرهان أن تكون ضرورية أو منتهية إليها ولكان أكثر المصادرات الهندسية نظرية، إلى غير ذلك من المفاسد كما لا يخفى على المتدرب، هذا والله أعلم بالصواب. (١) ولم أجد في كلام الدواني في شرح التهذيب هذا الذي نقله عنه الشارح، ولا في حاشية الشمسية، ولعله في كتاب آخر له، والله أعلم.
Either first: dividing knowledge into concept and assent by way of acquired (hadith) occurrence, or second: dividing them into necessary and theoretical by way of the occurring concept and assent, and no attention is paid to the double specification, and that is the more apparent. And what is said: that the knowledge of the Necessary Exalted is not concept and assent, if it is intended that He Most High is not an assenter to true propositions, as appears from the Four Journeys, then it is false, rather it is explicit disbelief. And if it is intended merely terminological convention due to the lack of scientific interest in eternal knowledge, then there is no dispute in it, but it does not necessarily imply that eternal knowledge is not concept and assent. He said in ‘al-Hashiya’: The intuitive and the theoretical are attributes of knowledge, rather the originated knowledge, and from that they permitted for the possessor of the holy power that all theoretical things are conceptive necessary for him, so it cannot be objected that something is theoretical for one person and intuitive for another, so there is no meaning to dependence. The way of rebuttal: that the knowledge of each one is individually different from another knowledge, so it is permissible that one depends and the other does not. And it might be answered by manipulation in the meaning of dependence, so reflect. This is based on the fact that the essentially acquired is the knowledge. And the verifiers, among them al-Sayyid (may Allah sanctify his noble secret), held that the essentially acquired is the known object, and it is apparent to whoever consults his conscience; for the purpose of definition, for example, is the attainment of the quiddity of man by any individual of the individuals of knowledge, so then there is no answer except the latter. Its detail: that the intended meaning of dependence is not real dependence, but rather the matter that necessitates the entry of the fa’, even if its attainment is possible without it, and some relied on the common usage of dependence in this sense in their speech; for they allowed the exchange of independent cause on a single individual effect, while using the word dependence therein, despite the possibility of the effect existing without each one of them. And the answer is not dependent on this as was thought; for this is a gross error. And this noble thinker said in the answer that the intended meaning in the definition of the acquired from ‘occurrence’ is absolute occurrence, and in the definition of the necessary is the absolute occurrence, so the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection, and the necessary is that all aspects of whose occurrences do not depend on reflection, so what is obtained for one by reflection is always theoretical, even if another is obtained without reflection, and the necessary is what is obtained for everyone without reflection(1). And it is not hidden what is in it; for if it was his own convention, then no dispute, but the problem remains on what is established with the people. And if he claims that the intended meaning of the people is this as apparent from his speech, then it is false, otherwise the following proof would not be complete, and their statement ‘the principles of demonstration must be necessary or terminating to it’ would not be correct, and most geometrical postulates would be theoretical, and other corruptions as is not hidden from the trained. This, and Allah knows best what is correct. (1) And I did not find in the speech of al-Dawani in his commentary on al-Tahdhib this which the commentator transmitted from him, nor in the Hashiya on al-Shamsiyya, perhaps it is in another book of his. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a compressed matn line from al-Sullam about the division of knowledge. The author first states that knowledge can be divided either first into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq), or second into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nadari). He notes that the preferred view is not to mind the double classification. He then addresses an objection about divine knowledge: some claimed Allah's knowledge is not concept and assent. He refutes this, saying if it means Allah does not assent to truths, it is disbelief; if it's just terminology, it's permissible but does not negate that His knowledge could be called concept and assent. He cites a hashia stating that 'intuitive' and 'theoretical' apply only to originated knowledge, not eternal. This allows that for a person with holy power (like a prophet), all theoretical matters may be intuitive, so something can be theoretical for one person and intuitive for another without contradiction. The rebuttal is that each person's knowledge is individually distinct, so one may depend on reflection and another not. Next, the author discusses a deeper issue: whether the essentially acquired thing in knowledge acquisition is the knowledge itself or the known object. The verifiers (muhaqqiqun, including al-Sayyid) hold it is the known object, as the purpose of definition is to attain the quiddity, not the knowledge. He then clarifies the meaning of 'dependence' (tawaqquf) in the definitions: it is not real dependence but a conditional necessity (like the entry of 'fa' in a conditional statement). Some scholars allowed independent causes for a single effect while still using 'dependence' loosely. The author criticizes a certain thinker's proposed solution that the theoretical is that whose occurrence in sum depends on reflection and the necessary is that all aspects of which do not depend. He dismisses this as a mere terminological change that fails to solve the real issue, because if taken as the people's intended meaning, it would break the standard proof that the principles of demonstration must be necessary, and would render most geometrical postulates theoretical, leading to absurdities. The author concludes with 'Allah knows best,' and a footnote notes that the attributed view of al-Dawani is not found in his works.

Key Terms
التوقف
الحقيقي
الفاء
العلة المستقلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the intended meaning of 'tawaqquf' (dependence) in the definition of theoretical knowledge?
A) Real causal dependence
B) Temporal sequence
C) Conditional necessity, like the 'fa' in a conditional statement
D) Logical requirement that is impossible to violate

Key Takeaway
Dependence in logic means conditional necessity, not efficient causality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Use the reinterpretation of tawaqquf to explain: 'Knowledge of Allah's existence depends on reflection for a common person but not for a prophet.' Write a statement showing the conditional nature.

Critique of a Redefinition of Necessary and Theoretical
Author criticizes a proposed redefinition of necessary/theoretical that fails the test of established usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and critique a flawed redefinition of necessary/theoretical that fails because it treats individual variation as a matter of terminology.

Core Idea
Redefining necessary/theoretical as relative to each person breaks the standard proof.

The passage concludes with a critique of a certain thinker's attempt to solve the problem of individual variation by redefining necessary and theoretical. According to that thinker, theoretical is what depends on reflection 'in sum' and necessary is what does not depend 'in all aspects'. The author rejects this as a mere terminological change that does not align with the established meaning, and that it leads to absurd consequences like making geometrical postulates theoretical. This lesson will help you evaluate such redefinitions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the proposed redefinition
The thinker says: 'النظري ما يتوقف حصول في الجملة على النظر، والضروري ما لا يتوقف جميع أنحاء حصولاته على النظر' — theoretical is what depends in sum, necessary is what does not depend in all aspects.
2
Identify the author's objection
The author says if this is just the thinker's own convention, there's no dispute. But if he claims it's what the people (logicians) meant, it's false. Because it would make many self-evident principles theoretical.
3
Understand the consequences
The author gives examples: the principles of demonstration are supposed to be necessary, but under this redefinition they would be theoretical. Also, geometrical postulates would become theoretical, which is absurd.

Critique of definitions of kasbi and daruri
Author critiques a scholar's definitions of kasbi and daruri as mistaken and leading to contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical flaw in a non-standard definition of daruri and kasbi and evaluate its consequences for demonstrative sciences.

Core Idea
A definition of 'necessary' that makes it depend on the individual is a corruption of the foundations of demonstration.

In this passage, the author critiques a scholar's redefinition of necessary (daruri) and acquired (kasbi) knowledge. The scholar's definitions, while seemingly plausible, lead to unacceptable consequences for the certainty of demonstrative sciences. The author shows how the scholar's error stems from misinterpreting the term 'tawaqquf' and the conventional usage among logicians. This lesson will walk you through the critique and help you assess why definitions must conform to the established technical lexicon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar's definitions
What does the scholar propose as the meaning of kasbi and daruri? Note that he defines kasbi as 'absolute attaining' and daruri as 'absolute attainment' such that theoretical knowledge depends on consideration in general, while necessary knowledge does not depend in any aspect.
The scholar's definitions shift the criterion from dependence on consideration to individual variability.
2
Locate the author's objection to 'tawaqquf'
The author criticizes the scholar's understanding of 'tawaqquf' (dependence). The scholar's usage allows for multiple independent causes for a single effect, which contradicts the standard logical meaning.
'Tawaqquf' here refers to the dependence of knowledge on consideration.
3
Examine the absurd consequences
The author draws out consequences: if the scholar's definitions were accepted, then the principles of demonstration would not be necessary, and most geometrical postulates would become theoretical. This is unacceptable.
The author uses a reductio ad absurdum: the definition leads to contradictions with established truths.
4
Determine why the definitions are false within the system
The author argues that if the scholar were using his own terminology, there would be no quarrel, but within the established conventional usage, his definitions are false. They do not uphold the necessary character of first principles.
The key is that definitions must match the technical lexicon of the discipline.
5
Summarize the logical principle at stake
Arbitrary redefinitions of technical terms can destroy the entire edifice of demonstrative knowledge. Definitions must be internally consistent and consistent with the established framework.
This lesson underscores the importance of terminological discipline in Islamic logic.

تقسيم العلم إلى تصور وتصديق. التوقف بهذا المعنى في كلامهم؛ فإنهم جوزوا تبادل العلة المستقلة على معلول واحد شخصي، مع إطلاق لفظ التوقف فيها، مع إمكان وجود المعلول بدون كل واحد منها، وليس الجواب موقوفا على هذا كما ظن؛ فإن هذا غلط فاحش. وقال هذا الظان الجليل في الجواب إن المراد في تعريف الكسبي من الحصول مطلق الحصول، وفي تعريف الضروري الحصول المطلق، فالنظري ما يتوقف حصول في الجملة على النظر، والضروري ما لا يتوقف جميع أنحاء حصولاته على النظر، فما يحصل لواحد بالنظر يكون نظريا دائما، وإن حصل آخر بلا نظر، وإنما الضروري ما يحصل لكل واحد من غير نظر. ولا يخفى ما فيه؛ إذ لو كان هو المصطلح من عند نفسه فلا مشاحة، لكن الإشكال باق على ما هو مقرر عند القوم. وإن زعم أن مراد القوم هو هذا كما هو ظاهر كلامه فباطل، وإلا لم يتم الدليل الآتي، ولا يستقيم قولهم: مبادئ البرهان أن تكون ضرورية أو منتهية إليها، ولكان أكثر المصادرات الهندسية نظرية، إلى غير ذلك من المفاسد.
Division of knowledge into concept and assent. Tawaqquf in this sense in their speech: for they allowed substitution of independent cause for a single individual effect, while using the word 'tawaqquf' despite the possibility of the effect existing without each of them. And the answer is not dependent on this as he thought; for this is a grievous error. And this venerable presumptuous one said in answer that what is meant in the definition of acquired [knowledge] from 'attaining' is absolute attaining, and in the definition of necessary [knowledge] is absolute attainment. So theoretical [knowledge] is that whose attainment depends in general on consideration, and necessary is that whose attainment in all its aspects does not depend on consideration. So what is attained by one through consideration is always theoretical, even if another attainment occurs without consideration. Rather, necessary is what is attained by everyone without consideration. And it is not hidden what is in it; for if he had made his own terminology then there is no dispute, but the problem remains according to what is established among the people. And if he claims that the people's intention is this, as is apparent from his speech, it is false; otherwise the following proof would not be complete, nor would their saying 'the principles of demonstration must be necessary or lead to them' be sound, and most geometric postulates would become theoretical, among other corruptions.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement of a previous scholar's definitions of necessary (daruri) and acquired (kasbi) knowledge. The author begins by stating that the division of knowledge into concept and assent is accepted, but the problem lies in the understanding of 'tawaqquf' (dependence). The author accuses the scholar of error, then reports the scholar's proposed definitions: in the definition of acquired knowledge, 'attaining' is absolute, while in necessary knowledge it is also absolute, leading to a distinction where theoretical knowledge depends on consideration in general and necessary knowledge does not depend in any aspect. The author rejects this, arguing that if the scholar were using his own terminology there would be no quarrel, but the problem persists within the established conventional terminology. Moreover, if the scholar's interpretation were correct, it would undermine key proofs: the principles of demonstration would not be necessarily true, and geometrical axioms would become theoretical, which is absurd. The argument is evaluated in terms of its consequences within the tradition of Islamic logic.

Key Terms
توقف (tawaqquf): Dependence of one cognitive state on another; here critiqued as allowing multiple independent causes for a single effect.
كسبي (kasbi): Acquired knowledge; opposed to daruri (necessary). The scholar defines it as absolute obtaining, which the author rejects.
ضروري (daruri): Necessary knowledge that does not depend on consideration in any aspect; the author argues this is not the standard definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what problem arises if we accept the scholar's definition that all geometric postulates are theoretical?
A) They would not be necessary principles for demonstration.
B) They would be acquired by everyone without consideration.
C) They would be known by instinct.
D) They would be self-evident.

Key Takeaway
Definitions in logic must adhere to established technical usage; arbitrary redefinitions undermine the certainty of the entire demonstrative system.

The Division of Knowledge into Necessary and Theoretical
Author states the division and argues that not all concepts are necessary nor all theoretical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define necessary and theoretical knowledge and explain why not all concepts and assents are self-evident.

Core Idea
Knowledge is not all self-evident; some must be acquired through reasoning.

This passage establishes a fundamental division in epistemology: knowledge is either necessary (self-evident) or theoretical (acquired through reasoning). The author argues against the extreme view that all knowledge is self-evident, pointing out that if that were true, no intellectual acquisition would be needed. This sets the stage for the necessity of logic as a tool for theoretical knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Find the terms necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari) in the Arabic. Understand what each entails.
Necessary knowledge does not require reasoning; theoretical knowledge does.
2
Locate the two claims being refuted
The author states that not every concept is necessary and not every assent is necessary. Note the shared proof.
The phrase 'ليس الكل من كل منهما بديهيا' captures both claims.
3
Examine the argument against all knowledge being necessary
If all were necessary, acquisition (kasb) would be unnecessary. But we know acquisition exists, so the claim is false for assent; for concept, it is contested by al-Razi.
The author will later refute al-Razi's doubt.
4
Understand the importance of the division
This division shows that logic is needed to acquire theoretical knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقسيم كل من التصور والتصديق إلى ضروري ونظري. وليس الكل من كل منهما بديهيا غير متوقف على النظر، إشارة إلى دعويين، أي ليس كل واحد من التصور ضروريا، وكذا التصديق، والتصديق إلى البديهي جمعهما في عبارة واحدة؛ للاشتراك في الدليل؛ اختصارا في العبارة. وإلا، أي وإن كان الكل ضروريا فأنت مستغن عن الاكتساب. وبطلان التالي في التصديق ظاهر، وأما في التصور فممنوع عند الإمام وسيأتي كشف شبهه. ولا نظريا متوقفا على النظر، وإلا لما حصل شيء من العلوم؛ لأن النظر فعل اختياري، فلا بد من التصديق بالفائدة، والتصور بوجه ما، وهو أيضا نظري، فلا بد في اكتسابه منهما أيضا، وهكذا. وأيضا لو كان الكل نظريا لدار، فيلزم تقدم الشيء على نفسه بمرتبتين، الدور إن كان بمرتبة فيكون التوقف على نفسه بمرتبتين.
Division of each of concept and assent into necessary and theoretical. And not all of each of them is self-evident, independent of consideration, indicating two claims: i.e., not every concept is necessary, nor every assent. He combined them in one phrase due to the commonality of the proof, to shorten the expression. Otherwise, i.e., if all were necessary, then you would be independent of acquisition. The falsity of the consequent in assent is apparent; but regarding concept, it is disputed by al-Imam [al-Razi], and his doubt will be uncovered later. And [they are] not all theoretical, dependent on consideration; otherwise nothing of the sciences would be attained, because consideration is an act of choice, so there must be assent to the benefit, and concept in some way, and that too is theoretical, so its acquisition would require both of them, and so on. Also, if all were theoretical, there would be circularity, so the thing would precede itself by two ranks: if the circularity is by one rank, then the dependence on itself is by two ranks.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and argumentative section that divides both concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq) into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari). The author asserts that not all concepts are self-evident (badihi), nor all assents. He combines both claims due to a shared argument. He then considers the extreme possibilities: if all knowledge were necessary, we would not need acquisition (kasb); this is obviously false for assent, and contested for concept by Imam al-Razi (whose objection will be refuted later). Conversely, if all knowledge were theoretical, then nothing would be known because theoretical knowledge requires a prior concept and assent, leading to an infinite regress or circularity. The author explains that consideration (nazar) is an act of choice, so it must itself be based on some already-existing knowledge; if that too is theoretical, we have a vicious circle. If the circle has one degree, then a thing would depend on itself with two degrees of separation. This argument establishes that knowledge must have a foundation in self-evident truths.

Key Terms
تصور
تصديق
بديهي
نظري

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because al-Razi disputes it.
B) Because if all were necessary, acquisition would be unnecessary.
C) Because concepts are always theoretical.
D) Because the Quran says so.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge is divided into necessary and theoretical; not all is self-evident, otherwise reasoning would be pointless.

Why Knowledge Cannot Be Entirely Theoretical
Author states the division and argues that not all concepts are necessary nor all theoretical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the circularity argument against the claim that all knowledge is theoretical and apply it to Islamic science.

Core Idea
If all knowledge were theoretical, we would need prior knowledge to start, leading to an impossible infinite regress.

The author now turns to the opposite extreme: if all knowledge were theoretical, then each act of reasoning would require prior knowledge, leading to circularity or infinite regress. This argument is crucial because it shows that there must be a foundation of self-evident truths. Otherwise, no science, including the Islamic sciences, could ever begin.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hypothetical scenario
What does it mean for all knowledge to be theoretical? It means every piece of knowledge depends on a process of reasoning.
2
Trace the regress
If all knowledge is theoretical, then the first act of reasoning requires prior knowledge. But that prior knowledge would also be theoretical, requiring more prior knowledge, ad infinitum.
3
Identify the consequence
The author says that if all were theoretical, nothing would be attained. Because consideration is an act of choice, it must be based on some benefit known via concept and assent, which themselves would be theoretical, leading to infinite regress.
4
Recognize the circularity
The argument also states that if the regress is cyclic (circularity), the thing would depend on itself, which is impossible.
5
Conclude the necessity of self-evident knowledge
Therefore, some knowledge must be necessary (self-evident) to avoid this problem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He combined them in one phrase due to the commonality of the proof, to shorten the expression. Otherwise, i.e., if all were necessary, then you would be independent of acquisition. The Division of Knowledge: Necessary and Theoretical
Author states the division and argues against all being necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari) knowledge and explain why not all knowledge can be necessary.

Core Idea
Knowledge requires a foundation of self-evident truths to avoid infinite regress.

This passage introduces one of the most fundamental distinctions in Islamic logic and epistemology: the division of knowledge into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari). The author argues that not all knowledge can be necessary, because if it were, we would have no need for acquisition and inference — a position that is clearly false. However, there is a famous dispute: Imam al-Razi held that all conceptual knowledge is self-evident. Understanding this division is key to grasping how proofs are structured in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two kinds of knowledge
Locate the terms 'daruri' (ضروري) and 'nazari' (نظري) in the Arabic. The passage divides both concepts (tasawwur) and assents (tasdiq) into these two categories.
Notice that the division applies to both types of knowledge.
2
Extract the two claims
The author says the phrase 'not all are self-evident' actually contains two claims: not every concept is necessary, and not every assent is necessary. Separate them in your mind.
3
Analyze the conditional argument
The author uses a conditional: 'If all were necessary, then you would be independent of acquisition (istighna' 'an al-iktisab).' The consequent is false, so the antecedent must be false. This is a modus tollens argument.
The falsity of the consequent in assent is said to be 'apparent' (zahir), but disputed for concepts.
4
Understand al-Razi's objection
Imam al-Razi disagreed regarding concepts, claiming all concepts are self-evident. The author promises to refute this later, so note that this issue is not settled here.
This shows that the division is not merely definitional but involves substantive debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَنْ تَقْسِيمَ كُلٌّ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرِ وَالتَّصْدِيقِ إِلَى ضَرُورِي وَنَظَرِي وَلَيْسَ الْكُلُّ مِنْ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا بَدِيهِيَّا غَيْرَ مُتَوَقِّفٍ عَلَى النَّظْرِ إشارة إلى دعويين أي ليس كل واحد من التصور ضروريا وكذا التصديق جمعهما في عبارة واحدة للاشتراك في الدليل اختصارا في العبارة والنظري وإلا أي وإن كان الكل ضروريا فأنت مستغن عن الاكتساب وبطلان التالي في التصديق ظاهر وأما في التصور فممنوع عند الإمام وسيأتي كشف شبهه إن شاء الله تعالى
That the division of each of concept and assent into necessary and theoretical, and not all of each of them are self-evident not dependent on reflection, is an indication of two claims: that not every concept is necessary, and similarly for assent. He combined them in one phrase due to shared evidence, as brevity in expression. And the theoretical. And otherwise, i.e. if all were necessary, then you would be independent of acquisition. The falsity of the consequent in assent is apparent, but as for concept, it is disputed by the Imam (al-Razi) and his doubt will be revealed later, God willing.

This passage defines the division of knowledge into necessary (daruri) and theoretical (nazari) for both concepts (tasawwur) and assents (tasdiq). The author explains that the statement is actually two claims, combined for brevity. He then argues that not all can be necessary, because if all were, then acquisition of knowledge would be unnecessary, which is false. However, he notes that Imam al-Razi disagreed regarding concepts, claiming all concepts are self-evident. The author promises to refute this later. This sets up the need for a mix of necessary and theoretical knowledge.

Condition of Assent's Dependence on Conception
Author discusses a completion on the dependence of assent on conception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition under which the dependence of assent on conception holds and evaluate its applicability.

Core Idea
Assent depends on conception only if all conceptions are acquired.

In this passage, the author presents a completion by later scholars who assert that if no conception occurs, no assent occurs. However, he immediately qualifies this: it only holds if all conceptions are themselves acquired (kasbi). If some conceptions are necessary (daruri), the dependence may not be universal. This distinction is crucial for understanding the epistemological foundations of Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Find the statement: 'إذا لم يحصل تصور لم يحصل تصديق'. This is the claim that assent is dependent on conception.
2
Find the condition
Look for the phrase 'إنما يتم لو فرض كسبية جميع التصورات أيضا'. This says the claim holds only if all conceptions are acquired.
3
Analyze the alternative
Consider the opposite: if some conceptions are necessary (daruri) and all assents are acquired, then the original claim does not hold. Why? Because necessary conceptions are not preceded by any other conception.
Necessary conceptions are foundational and do not require prior acquisition.
4
Apply to Islamic science
Reflect: In fiqh, the conception of 'obligation' is foundational. Is it acquired or necessary? If it is necessary, then the dependence of assent on conception may not apply in all cases.
This affects how we understand the epistemology of legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كنها لنفسه، فلم يحصل تصور . وتممه بعض الأجلة من المتأخرين، وقال: إذا لم يحصل تصور لم يحصل تصديق ؛ لأن التصديق متوقف على التصور. ولا يخفى أن هذا إنما يتم لو فرض كسبية جميع التصورات أيضا ، أما لو فرض كسبية التصديقات بأسرها مع ضرورية بعض التصورات فلا يتم ذلك. قال بعض من الأجلة: إن الوجه في علم الشيء بالوجه لا يتصور بالكنه ولا بالوجه وإلا لكان المقصود بالعرض مقصودا بالذات والمتصور بالذات متصورا بالعرض في ملاحظة واحدة، بل الوجه في علم الشيء بالوجه يحصل كنهه بحيث يكون مرآة لملاحظة ذي الوجه ، فحينئذ يجوز أن يحصل كنه الوجه في أزمنة غير متناهية من مباديه. وبالجملة ما ذكر في امتناع التصور بالكنه مسلم، وفي امتناع التصور بالوجه غير مسلم، ولا يخفى ما فيه من الاختلال، أما أولا : فلأنه لا على شيء من مقدماته ، اللهم إلا أن يكون معارضة ، وأما ثانيا فلأن العلم بكنه الشيء مختص بالضروريات عنده، فلا يمكن على تقدير نظرية الكل. نعم، يرد عليه أن يكون مبادئ الكنه والوجه مشتركة ؛ فإن ما هو ذاتي لشيء عرضي لوجهه، وما هو ذاتي لوجهه يجوز أن يكون عرضيا لذلك الشيء، والله أعلم.
It [the thing] is not known by its essence, so no conception occurs. And some of the later eminent scholars completed it, saying: If no conception occurs, no assent occurs, because assent is dependent on conception. It is not hidden that this only holds if it is assumed that all conceptions are also acquired; but if it is assumed that all assents are acquired while some conceptions are necessary, then it does not hold. Some of the eminent scholars said: Indeed, the aspect in knowledge of a thing by the aspect is not conceived by the essence nor by the aspect; otherwise, the intended accidentally would be intended essentially, and that which is conceived essentially would be conceived accidentally in one observation. Rather, the aspect in knowledge of a thing by the aspect is such that its essence is obtained as a mirror for observing the thing having the aspect. Then it is permissible that the essence of the aspect be obtained in infinite times from its principles. In summary, what was mentioned regarding the impossibility of conception by essence is accepted, while the impossibility of conception by aspect is not accepted. Yet the disturbance in it is not hidden. First, because it does not rely on any of its premises, unless it is a counterargument. Second, because knowledge of the essence of a thing is specific to necessary [conceptions] according to him, so it is impossible given the supposition that all [conceptions] are theoretical. Yes, it is objected that the principles of the essence and the aspect are common; for what is essential to a thing is accidental to its aspect, and what is essential to its aspect may be accidental to that thing. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a previous statement that something is not known by its essence, so no conception of it occurs. The author first presents a completion by later scholars: they argue that if no conception occurs, then no assent occurs, because assent depends on conception. However, the author notes that this only holds if all conceptions are assumed to be acquired (kasbi). If some conceptions are necessary (daruri), then the dependency does not necessarily apply. Then another scholar is quoted: the 'aspect' (wajh) in knowing a thing by its aspect is not itself conceived by essence or by aspect; otherwise it would lead to confusion between essential and accidental intention. Rather, the aspect serves as a mirror through which the thing is observed, and its essence may be obtained in infinite time from its principles. The author then critiques: the impossibility of conception by essence is accepted, but the impossibility by aspect is not accepted, for two reasons: first, the argument against it does not stand on its own premises, unless it is a counterargument; second, the knowledge of the essence of a thing, according to that scholar, is restricted to necessary conceptions, so it cannot hold if all are theoretical. Furthermore, the principles of essence and aspect are shared, and what is essential to one may be accidental to the other. The passage ends with a humble 'And God knows best.'

تصديق
كسبي
ضروري

A) Only if all assents are necessary.
B) Only if all conceptions are acquired.
C) Only if some conceptions are necessary.
D) Always holds without condition.

Key Takeaway
The dependence of assent on conception is conditional; it applies only when all conceptions are acquired, not when some are necessary.
